dq,\n378:                                               long timestamp,\n379:                                               byte[] key,\n380:                                               byte[] value,\n381:                                               Header[] headers,\n382:                                               AppendCallbacks callbacks,\n383:                                               ByteBuffer buffer,\n384:                                               long nowMs) {\n385:         assert partition != RecordMetadata.UNKNOWN_PARTITION;\n386: \n387:         RecordAppendResult appendResult = tryAppend(timestamp, key, value, headers, callbacks, dq, nowMs);\n388:         if (appendResult != null) {\n389:             // Somebody else found us a batch, return the one we waited for! Hopefully this doesn't happen often...\n390:             return appendResult;\n391:         }\n392: \n393:         MemoryRecordsBuilder recordsBuilder = recordsBuilder(buffer);\n394:         ProducerBatch batch = new ProducerBatch(new TopicPartition(topic, partition), recordsBuilder, nowMs);\n395:         FutureRecordMetadata future = Objects.requireNonNull(batch.tryAppend(timestamp, key, value, headers,\n396:                 callbacks, nowMs));\n397: \n398:         dq.addLast(batch);\n399:         incomplete.add(batch);\n400: \n401:         return new RecordAppendResult(future, dq.size() > 1 || batch.isFull(), true, batch.estimatedSizeInBytes());\n402:     }\n403: \n404:     private MemoryRecordsBuilder recordsBuilder(ByteBuffer buffer) {\n405:         return MemoryRecords.builder(buffer, RecordBatch.CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE, compression, TimestampType.CREATE_TIME, 0L);\n406:     }\n407: \n408:     /**\n409:      * Check if all batches in the queue are full.\n410:      */\n411:     private boolean allBatchesFull(Deque<ProducerBatch> deque) {\n412:         // Only the last batch may be incomplete, so we just check that.\n413:         ProducerBatch last = deque.peekLast();\n414:         return last == null || last.isFull();\n415:     }\n416: \n417:      /**\n418:      *  Try to append to a ProducerBatch.\n419:      *\n420:      *  If it is full, we return null and a new batch is created. We also close the batch for record appends to free up\n421:      *  resources like compression buffers. The batch will be fully closed (ie. the record batch headers will be written\n422:      *  and memory records built) in one of the following cases (whichever comes first): right before send,\n423:      *  if it is expired, or when the producer is closed.\n424:      */\n425:     private RecordAppendResult tryAppend(long timestamp, byte[] key, byte[] value, Header[] headers,\n426:                                          Callback callback, Deque<ProducerBatch> deque, long nowMs) {\n427:         if (closed)\n428:             throw new KafkaException(\"Producer closed while send in progress\");\n429:         ProducerBatch last = deque.peekLast();\n430:         if (last != null) {\n431:             int initialBytes = last.estimatedSizeInBytes();\n432:             FutureRecordMetadata future = last.tryAppend(timestamp, key, value, headers, callback, nowMs);\n433:             if (future == null) {\n434:                 last.closeForRecordAppends();\n435:             } else {\n436:                 int appendedBytes = last.estimatedSizeInBytes() - initialBytes;\n437:                 return new RecordAppendResult(future, deque.size() > 1 || last.isFull(), false, appendedBytes);\n438:             }\n439:         }\n440:         return null;\n441:     }\n442: \n443:     private boolean isMuted(TopicPartition tp) {\n444:         return muted.contains(tp);\n445:     }\n446: \n447:     public void resetNextBatchExpiryTime() {\n448:         nextBatchExpiryTimeMs = Long.MAX_VALUE;\n449:     }\n450: \n451:     public void maybeUpdateNextBatchExpiryTime(ProducerBatch batch) {\n452:         if (batch.createdMs + deliveryTimeoutMs  > 0) {\n453:             // the non-negative check is to guard us against potential overflow due to setting\n454:             // a large value for deliveryTimeoutMs\n455:             nextBatchExpiryTimeMs = Math.min(nextBatchExpiryTimeMs, batch.createdMs + deliveryTimeoutMs);\n456:         } else {\n457:             log.warn(\"Skipping next batch expiry time update due to addition overflow: \"\n458:                 + \"batch.createMs={}, deliveryTimeoutMs={}\", batch.createdMs, deliveryTimeoutMs);\n459:         }\n460:     }\n461: \n462:     /**\n463:      * Get a list of batches which have been sitting in the accumulator too long and need to be expired.\n464:      */\n465:     public List<ProducerBatch> expiredBatches(long now) {\n466:         List<ProducerBatch> expiredBatches = new ArrayList<>();\n467:         for (TopicInfo topicInfo : topicInfoMap.values()) {\n468:             for (Deque<ProducerBatch> deque : topicInfo.batches.values()) {\n469:                 // expire the batches in the order of sending\n470:                 synchronized (deque) {\n471:                     while (!deque.isEmpty()) {\n472:                         ProducerBatch batch = deque.getFirst();\n473:                         if (batch.hasReachedDeliveryTimeout(deliveryTimeoutMs, now)) {\n474:                             deque.poll();\n475:                             batch.abortRecordAppends();\n476:                             expiredBatches.add(batch);\n477:                         } else {\n478:                             maybeUpdateNextBatchExpiryTime(batch);\n479:                             break;\n480:                         }\n481:                     }\n482:                 }\n483:             }\n484:         }\n485:         return expiredBatches;\n486:     }\n487: \n488:     public long getDeliveryTimeoutMs() {\n489:         return deliveryTimeoutMs;\n490:     }\n491: \n492:     /**\n493:      * Re-enqueue the given record batch in the accumulator. In Sender.completeBatch method, we check\n494:      * whether the batch has reached deliveryTimeoutMs or not. Hence we do not do the delivery timeout check here.\n495:      */\n496:     public void reenqueue(ProducerBatch batch, long now) {\n497:         batch.reenqueued(now);\n498:         Deque<ProducerBatch> deque = getOrCreateDeque(batch.topicPartition);\n499:         synchronized (deque) {\n500:             if (transactionManager != null)\n501:                 insertInSequenceOrder(deque, batch);\n502:             else\n503:                 deque.addFirst(batch);\n504:         }\n505:     }\n506: \n507:     /**\n508:      * Split the big batch that has been rejected and reenqueue the split batches in to the accumulator.\n509:      * @return the number of split batches.\n510:      */\n511:     public int splitAndReenqueue(ProducerBatch bigBatch) {\n512:         // Reset the estimated compression ratio to the initial value or the big batch compression ratio, whichever\n513:         // is bigger. There are several different ways to do the reset. We chose the most conservative one to ensure\n514:         // the split doesn't happen too often.\n515:         CompressionRatioEstimator.setEstimation(bigBatch.topicPartition.topic(), compression.type(),\n516:                                                 Math.max(1.0f, (float) bigBatch.compressionRatio()));\n517:         Deque<ProducerBatch> dq = bigBatch.split(this.batchSize);\n518:         int numSplitBatches = dq.size();\n519:         Deque<ProducerBatch> partitionDequeue = getOrCreateDeque(bigBatch.topicPartition);\n520:         while (!dq.isEmpty()) {\n521:             ProducerBatch batch = dq.pollLast();\n522:             incomplete.add(batch);\n523:             // We treat the newly split batches as if they are not even tried.\n524:             synchronized (partitionDequeue) {\n525:                 if (transactionManager != null) {\n526:                     // We should track the newly created batches since they already have assigned sequences.\n527:                     transactionManager.addInFlightBatch(batch);\n528:                     insertInSequenceOrder(partitionDequeue, batch);\n529:                 } else {\n530:                     partitionDequeue.addFirst(batch);\n531:                 }\n532:             }\n533:         }\n534:         return numSplitBatches;\n535:     }\n536: \n537:     // We will have to do extra work to ensure the queue is in order when requests are being retried and there are\n538:     // multiple requests in flight to that partition. If the first in flight request fails to append, then all the\n539:     // subsequent in flight requests will also fail because the sequence numbers will not be accepted.\n540:     //\n541:     // Further, once batches are being retried, we are reduced to a single in flight request for that partition. So when\n542:     // the subsequent batches come back in sequence order, they will have to be placed further back in the queue.\n543:     //\n544:     // Note that this assumes that all the batches in the queue which have an assigned sequence also have the current\n545:     // producer id. We will not attempt to reorder messages if the producer id has changed, we will throw an\n546:     // IllegalStateException instead.\n547:     private void insertInSequenceOrder(Deque<ProducerBatch> deque, ProducerBatch batch) {\n548:         // When we are re-enqueueing and have enabled idempotence, the re-enqueued batch must always have a sequence.\n549:         if (batch.baseSequence() == RecordBatch.NO_SEQUENCE)\n550:             throw new IllegalStateException(\"Trying to re-enqueue a batch which doesn't have a sequence even \" +\n551:                 \"though idempotency is enabled.\");\n552: \n553:         if (!transactionManager.hasInflightBatches(batch.topicPartition))\n554:             throw new IllegalStateException(\"We are re-enqueueing a batch which is not tracked as part of the in flight \" +\n555:                 \"requests. batch.topicPartition: \" + batch.topicPartition + \"; batch.baseSequence: \" + batch.baseSequence());\n556: \n557:         ProducerBatch firstBatchInQueue = deque.peekFirst();\n558:         if (firstBatchInQueue != null && firstBatchInQueue.hasSequence() && firstBatchInQueue.baseSequence() < batch.baseSequence()) {\n559:             // The incoming batch can't be inserted at the front of the queue without violating the sequence ordering.\n560:             // This means that the incoming batch should be placed somewhere further back.\n561:             // We need to find the right place for the incoming batch and insert it there.\n562:             // We will only enter this branch if we have multiple inflights sent to different brokers and we need to retry\n563:             // the inflight batches.\n564:             //\n565:             // Since we reenqueue exactly one batch a time and ensure that the queue is ordered by sequence always, it\n566:             // is a simple linear scan of a subset of the in flight batches to find the right place in the queue each time.\n567:             List<ProducerBatch> orderedBatches = new ArrayList<>();\n568:             while (deque.peekFirst() != null && deque.peekFirst().hasSequence() && deque.peekFirst().baseSequence() < batch.baseSequence())\n569:                 orderedBatches.add(deque.pollFirst());\n570: \n571:             log.debug(\"Reordered incoming batch with sequence {} for partition {}. It was placed in the queue at \" +\n572:                 \"position {}\", batch.baseSequence(), batch.topicPartition, orderedBatches.size());\n573:             // Either we have reached a point where there are batches without a sequence (ie. never been drained\n574:             // and are hence in order by default), or the batch at the front of the queue has a sequence greater\n575:             // than the incoming batch. This is the right place to add the incoming batch.\n576:             deque.addFirst(batch);\n577: \n578:             // Now we have to re insert the previously queued batches in the right order.\n579:             for (int i = orderedBatches.size() - 1; i >= 0; --i) {\n580:                 deque.addFirst(orderedBatches.get(i));\n581:             }\n582: \n583:             // At this point, the incoming batch has been queued in the correct place according to its sequence.\n584:         } else {\n585:             deque.addFirst(batch);\n586:         }\n587:     }\n588: \n589:     /**\n590:      * Add the leader to the ready nodes if the batch is ready\n591:      *\n592:      * @param exhausted 'true' is the buffer pool is exhausted\n593:      * @param part The partition\n594:      * @param leader The leader for the partition\n595:      * @param waitedTimeMs How long batch waited\n596:      * @param backingOff Is backing off\n597:      * @param backoffAttempts Number of attempts for calculating backoff delay\n598:      * @param full Is batch full\n599:      * @param nextReadyCheckDelayMs The delay for next check\n600:      * @param readyNodes The set of ready nodes (to be filled in)\n601:      * @return The delay for next check\n602:      */\n603:     private long batchReady(boolean exhausted, TopicPartition part, Node leader,\n604:                             long waitedTimeMs, boolean backingOff, int backoffAttempts,\n605:                             boolean full, long nextReadyCheckDelayMs, Set<Node> readyNodes) {\n606:         if (!readyNodes.contains(leader) && !isMuted(part)) {\n607:             long timeToWaitMs = backingOff ? retryBackoff.backoff(backoffAttempts > 0 ? backoffAttempts - 1 : 0) : lingerMs;\n608:             boolean expired = waitedTimeMs >= timeToWaitMs;\n609:             boolean transactionCompleting = transactionManager != null && transactionManager.isCompleting();\n610:             boolean sendable = full\n611:                     || expired\n612:                     || exhausted\n613:                     || closed\n614:                     || flushInProgress()\n615:                     || transactionCompleting;\n616:             if (sendable && !backingOff) {\n617:                 readyNodes.add(leader);\n618:             } else {\n619:                 long timeLeftMs = Math.max(timeToWaitMs - waitedTimeMs, 0);\n620:                 // Note that this results in a conservative estimate since an un-sendable partition may have\n621:                 // a leader that will later be found to have sendable data. However, this is good enough\n622:                 // since we'll just wake up and then sleep again for the remaining time.\n623:                 nextReadyCheckDelayMs = Math.min(timeLeftMs, nextReadyCheckDelayMs);\n624:             }\n625:         }\n626:         return nextReadyCheckDelayMs;\n627:     }\n628: \n629:     /**\n630:      * Iterate over partitions to see which one have batches ready and collect leaders of those\n631:      * partitions into the set of ready nodes.  If partition has no leader, add the topic to the set\n632:      * of topics with no leader.  This function also calculates stats for adaptive partitioning.\n633:      *\n634:      * @param metadataSnapshot      The cluster metadata\n635:      * @param nowMs                 The current time\n636:      * @param topic                 The topic\n637:      * @param topicInfo             The topic info\n638:      * @param nextReadyCheckDelayMs The delay for next check\n639:      * @param readyNodes            The set of ready nodes (to be filled in)\n640:      * @param unknownLeaderTopics   The set of topics with no leader (to be filled in)\n641:      * @return The delay for next check\n642:      */\n643:     private long partitionReady(MetadataSnapshot metadataSnapshot, long nowMs, String topic,\n644:                                 TopicInfo topicInfo,\n645:                                 long nextReadyCheckDelayMs, Set<Node> readyNodes, Set<String> unknownLeaderTopics) {\n646:         ConcurrentMap<Integer, Deque<ProducerBatch>> batches = topicInfo.batches;\n647:         // Collect the queue sizes for available partitions to be used in adaptive partitioning.\n648:         int[] queueSizes = null;\n649:         int[] partitionIds = null;\n650:         if (enableAdaptivePartitioning && batches.size() >= metadataSnapshot.cluster().partitionsForTopic(topic).size()) {\n651:             // We don't do adaptive partitioning until we scheduled at least a batch for all\n652:             // partitions (i.e. we have the corresponding entries in the batches map), we just\n653:             // do uniform.  The reason is that we build queue sizes from the batches map,\n654:             // and if an entry is missing in the batches map, then adaptive partitioning logic\n655:             // won't know about it and won't switch to it.\n656:             queueSizes = new int[batches.size()];\n657:             partitionIds = new int[queueSizes.length];\n658:         }\n659: \n660:         int queueSizesIndex = -1;\n661:         boolean exhausted = this.free.queued() > 0;\n662:         for (Map.Entry<Integer, Deque<ProducerBatch>> entry : batches.entrySet()) {\n663:             TopicPartition part = new TopicPartition(topic, entry.getKey());\n664:             // Advance queueSizesIndex so that we properly index available\n665:             // partitions.  Do it here so that it's done for all code paths.\n666: \n667:             Node leader = metadataSnapshot.cluster().leaderFor(part);\n668:             if (leader != null && queueSizes != null) {\n669:                 ++queueSizesIndex;\n670:                 assert queueSizesIndex < queueSizes.length;\n671:                 partitionIds[queueSizesIndex] = part.partition();\n672:             }\n673: \n674:             Deque<ProducerBatch> deque = entry.getValue();\n675: \n676:             final long waitedTimeMs;\n677:             final boolean backingOff;\n678:             final int backoffAttempts;\n679:             final int dequeSize;\n680:             final boolean full;\n681: \n682:             OptionalInt leaderEpoch = metadataSnapshot.leaderEpochFor(part);\n683: \n684:             // This loop is especially hot with large partition counts. So -\n685: \n686:             // 1. We should avoid code that increases synchronization between application thread calling\n687:             // send(), and background thread running runOnce(), see https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA-16226\n688: \n689:             // 2. We are careful to only perform the minimum required inside the\n690:             // synchronized block, as this lock is also used to synchronize producer threads\n691:             // attempting to append() to a partition/batch.\n692: \n693:             synchronized (deque) {\n694:                 // Deques are often empty in this path, esp with large partition counts,\n695:                 // so we exit early if we can.\n696:                 ProducerBatch batch = deque.peekFirst();\n697:                 if (batch == null) {\n698:                     continue;\n699:                 }\n700: \n701:                 waitedTimeMs = batch.waitedTimeMs(nowMs);\n702:                 batch.maybeUpdateLeaderEpoch(leaderEpoch);\n703:                 backingOff = shouldBackoff(batch.hasLeaderChangedForTheOngoingRetry(), batch, waitedTimeMs);\n704:                 backoffAttempts = batch.attempts();\n705:                 dequeSize = deque.size();\n706:                 full = dequeSize > 1 || batch.isFull();\n707:             }\n708: \n709:             if (leader == null) {\n710:                 // This is a partition for which leader is not known, but messages are available to send.\n711:                 // Note that entries are currently not removed from batches when deque is empty.\n712:                 unknownLeaderTopics.add(part.topic());\n713:             } else {\n714:                 if (queueSizes != null)\n715:                     queueSizes[queueSizesIndex] = dequeSize;\n716:                 if (partitionAvailabilityTimeoutMs > 0) {\n717:                     // Check if we want to exclude the partition from the list of available partitions\n718:                     // if the broker hasn't responded for some time.\n719:                     NodeLatencyStats nodeLatencyStats = nodeStats.get(leader.id());\n720:                     if (nodeLatencyStats != null) {\n721:                         // NOTE: there is no synchronization between reading metrics,\n722:                         // so we read ready time first to avoid accidentally marking partition\n723:                         // unavailable if we read while the metrics are being updated.\n724:                         long readyTimeMs = nodeLatencyStats.readyTimeMs;\n725:                         if (readyTimeMs - nodeLatencyStats.drainTimeMs > partitionAvailabilityTimeoutMs)\n726:                             --queueSizesIndex;\n727:                     }\n728:                 }\n729: \n730:                 nextReadyCheckDelayMs = batchReady(exhausted, part, leader, waitedTimeMs, backingOff,\n731:                     backoffAttempts, full, nextReadyCheckDelayMs, readyNodes);\n732:             }\n733:         }\n734: \n735:         // We've collected the queue sizes for partitions of this topic, now we can calculate\n736:         // load stats.  NOTE: the stats are calculated in place, modifying the\n737:         // queueSizes array.\n738:         topicInfo.builtInPartitioner.updatePartitionLoadStats(queueSizes, partitionIds, queueSizesIndex + 1);\n739:         return nextReadyCheckDelayMs;\n740:     }\n741: \n742:     /**\n743:      * Get a list of nodes whose partitions are ready to be sent, and the earliest time at which any non-sendable\n744:      * partition will be ready; Also return the flag for whether there are any unknown leaders for the accumulated\n745:      * partition batches.\n746:      * <p>\n747:      * A destination node is ready to send data if:\n748:      * <ol>\n749:      * <li>There is at least one partition that is not backing off its send\n750:      * <li><b>and</b> those partitions are not muted (to prevent reordering if\n751:      *   {@value org.apache.kafka.clients.producer.ProducerConfig#MAX_IN_FLIGHT_REQUESTS_PER_CONNECTION}\n752:      *   is set to one)</li>\n753:      * <li><b>and <i>any</i></b> of the following are true</li>\n754:      * <ul>\n755:      *     <li>The record set is full</li>\n756:      *     <li>The record set has sat in the accumulator for at least lingerMs milliseconds</li>\n757:      *     <li>The accumulator is out of memory and threads are blocking waiting for data (in this case all partitions\n758:      *     are immediately considered ready).</li>\n759:      *     <li>The accumulator has been closed</li>\n760:      * </ul>\n761:      * </ol>\n762:      */\n763:     public ReadyCheckResult ready(MetadataSnapshot metadataSnapshot, long nowMs) {\n764:         Set<Node> readyNodes = new HashSet<>();\n765:         long nextReadyCheckDelayMs = Long.MAX_VALUE;\n766:         Set<String> unknownLeaderTopics = new HashSet<>();\n767:         // Go topic by topic so that we can get queue sizes for partitions in a topic and calculate\n768:         // cumulative frequency table (used in partitioner).\n769:         for (Map.Entry<String, TopicInfo> topicInfoEntry : this.topicInfoMap.entrySet()) {\n770:             final String topic = topicInfoEntry.getKey();\n771:             nextReadyCheckDelayMs = partitionReady(metadataSnapshot, nowMs, topic, topicInfoEntry.getValue(), nextReadyCheckDelayMs, readyNodes, unknownLeaderTopics);\n772:         }\n773:         return new ReadyCheckResult(readyNodes, nextReadyCheckDelayMs, unknownLeaderTopics);\n774:     }\n775: \n776:     /**\n777:      * Check whether there are any batches which haven't been drained\n778:      */\n779:     public boolean hasUndrained() {\n780:         for (TopicInfo topicInfo : topicInfoMap.values()) {\n781:             for (Deque<ProducerBatch> deque : topicInfo.batches.values()) {\n782:                 synchronized (deque) {\n783:                     if (!deque.isEmpty())\n784:                         return true;\n785:                 }\n786:             }\n787:         }\n788:         return false;\n789:     }\n790: \n791:     private boolean shouldBackoff(boolean hasLeaderChanged, final ProducerBatch batch, final long waitedTimeMs) {\n792:         boolean shouldWaitMore = batch.attempts() > 0 && waitedTimeMs < retryBackoff.backoff(batch.attempts() - 1);\n793:         boolean shouldBackoff = !hasLeaderChanged && shouldWaitMore;\n794:         if (log.isTraceEnabled()) {\n795:             if (shouldBackoff) {\n796:                 log.trace(\n797:                     \"For {}, will backoff\", batch);\n798:             } else {\n799:                 log.trace(\n800:                     \"For {}, will not backoff, shouldWaitMore {}, hasLeaderChanged {}\", batch,\n801:                     shouldWaitMore, hasLeaderChanged);\n802:             }\n803:         } else if (log.isDebugEnabled() && hasLeaderChanged) {\n804:             // Add less-verbose log at DEBUG.\n805:             log.debug(\"For {}, leader has changed, hence skipping backoff.\", batch);\n806:         }\n807:         return shouldBackoff;\n808:     }\n809: \n810:     private boolean shouldStopDrainBatchesForPartition(ProducerBatch first, TopicPartition tp) {\n811:         ProducerIdAndEpoch producerIdAndEpoch;\n812:         if (transactionManager != null) {\n813:             if (!transactionManager.isSendToPartitionAllowed(tp))\n814:                 return true;\n815: \n816:             producerIdAndEpoch = transactionManager.producerIdAndEpoch();\n817:             if (!producerIdAndEpoch.isValid())\n818:                 // we cannot send the batch until we have refreshed the producer id\n819:                 return true;\n820: \n821:             if (!first.hasSequence()) {\n822:                 if (transactionManager.hasInflightBatches(tp) && transactionManager.hasStaleProducerIdAndEpoch(tp)) {\n823:                     // Don't drain any new batches while the partition has in-flight batches with a different epoch\n824:                     // and/or producer ID. Otherwise, a batch with a new epoch and sequence number\n825:                     // 0 could be written before earlier batches complete, which would cause out of sequence errors\n826:                     return true;\n827:                 }\n828: \n829:                 if (transactionManager.hasUnresolvedSequence(first.topicPartition))\n830:                     // Don't drain any new batches while the state of previous sequence numbers\n831:                     // is unknown. The previous batches would be unknown if they were aborted\n832:                     // on the client after being sent to the broker at least once.\n833:                     return true;\n834:             }\n835: \n836:             int firstInFlightSequence = transactionManager.firstInFlightSequence(first.topicPartition);\n837:             // If the queued batch already has an assigned sequence, then it is being retried.\n838:             // In this case, we wait until the next immediate batch is ready and drain that.\n839:             // We only move on when the next in line batch is complete (either successfully or due to\n840:             // a fatal broker error). This effectively reduces our in flight request count to 1.\n841:             return firstInFlightSequence != RecordBatch.NO_SEQUENCE && first.hasSequence()\n842:                     && first.baseSequence() != firstInFlightSequence;\n843:         }\n844:         return false;\n845:     }\n846: \n847:     private List<ProducerBatch> drainBatchesForOneNode(MetadataSnapshot metadataSnapshot, Node node, int maxSize, long now) {\n848:         int size = 0;\n849:         List<PartitionInfo> parts = metadataSnapshot.cluster().partitionsForNode(node.id());\n850:         List<ProducerBatch> ready = new ArrayList<>();\n851:         if (parts.isEmpty())\n852:             return ready;\n853:         /* to make starvation less likely each node has it's own drainIndex */\n854:         int drainIndex = getDrainIndex(node.idString());\n855:         int start = drainIndex = drainIndex % parts.size();\n856:         do {\n857:             PartitionInfo part = parts.get(drainIndex);\n858: \n859:             TopicPartition tp = new TopicPartition(part.topic(), part.partition());\n860:             updateDrainIndex(node.idString(), drainIndex);\n861:             drainIndex = (drainIndex + 1) % parts.size();\n862:             // Only proceed if the partition has no in-flight batches.\n863:             if (isMuted(tp))\n864:                 continue;\n865:             Deque<ProducerBatch> deque = getDeque(tp);\n866:             if (deque == null)\n867:                 continue;\n868: \n869:             OptionalInt leaderEpoch = metadataSnapshot.leaderEpochFor(tp);\n870: \n871:             final ProducerBatch batch;\n872:             synchronized (deque) {\n873:                 // invariant: !isMuted(tp,now) && deque != null\n874:                 ProducerBatch first = deque.peekFirst();\n875:                 if (first == null)\n876:                     continue;\n877: \n878:                 // first != null\n879:                 // Only drain the batch if it is not during backoff period.\n880:                 first.maybeUpdateLeaderEpoch(leaderEpoch);\n881:                 if (shouldBackoff(first.hasLeaderChangedForTheOngoingRetry(), first, first.waitedTimeMs(now)))\n882:                     continue;\n883: \n884:                 if (size + first.estimatedSizeInBytes() > maxSize && !ready.isEmpty()) {\n885:                     // there is a rare case that a single batch size is larger than the request size due to\n886:                     // compression; in this case we will still eventually send this batch in a single request\n887:                     break;\n888:                 } else {\n889:                     if (shouldStopDrainBatchesForPartition(first, tp))\n890:                         break;\n891:                 }\n892: \n893:                 batch = deque.pollFirst();\n894: \n895:                 boolean isTransactional = transactionManager != null && transactionManager.isTransactional();\n896:                 ProducerIdAndEpoch producerIdAndEpoch =\n897:                     transactionManager != null ? transactionManager.producerIdAndEpoch() : null;\n898:                 if (producerIdAndEpoch != null && !batch.hasSequence()) {\n899:                     // If the producer id/epoch of the partition do not match the latest one\n900:                     // of the producer, we update it and reset the sequence. This should be\n901:                     // only done when all its in-flight batches have completed. This is guarantee\n902:                     // in `shouldStopDrainBatchesForPartition`.\n903:                     transactionManager.maybeUpdateProducerIdAndEpoch(batch.topicPartition);\n904: \n905:                     // If the batch already has an assigned sequence, then we should not change the producer id and\n906:                     // sequence number, since this may introduce duplicates. In particular, the previous attempt\n907:                     // may actually have been accepted, and if we change the producer id and sequence here, this\n908:                     // attempt will also be accepted, causing a duplicate.\n909:                     //\n910:                     // Additionally, we update the next sequence number bound for the partition, and also have\n911:                     // the transaction manager track the batch so as to ensure that sequence ordering is maintained\n912:                     // even if we receive out of order responses.\n913:                     batch.setProducerState(producerIdAndEpoch, transactionManager.sequenceNumber(batch.topicPartition), isTransactional);\n914:                     transactionManager.incrementSequenceNumber(batch.topicPartition, batch.recordCount);\n915:                     log.debug(\"Assigned producerId {} and producerEpoch {} to batch with base sequence \" +\n916:                             \"{} being sent to partition {}\", producerIdAndEpoch.producerId,\n917:                         producerIdAndEpoch.epoch, batch.baseSequence(), tp);\n918: \n919:                     transactionManager.addInFlightBatch(batch);\n920:                 }\n921:             }\n922: \n923:             // the rest of the work by processing outside the lock\n924:             // close() is particularly expensive\n925:             batch.close();\n926:             size += batch.records().sizeInBytes();\n927:             ready.add(batch);\n928: \n929:             batch.drained(now);\n930:         } while (start != drainIndex);\n931:         return ready;\n932:     }\n933: \n934:     private int getDrainIndex(String idString) {\n935:         return nodesDrainIndex.computeIfAbsent(idString, s -> 0);\n936:     }\n937: \n938:     private void updateDrainIndex(String idString, int drainIndex) {\n939:         nodesDrainIndex.put(idString, drainIndex);\n940:     }\n941: \n942:     /**\n943:      * Drain all the data for the given nodes and collate them into a list of batches that will fit\n944:      * within the specified size on a per-node basis. This method attempts to avoid choosing the same\n945:      * topic-node over and over.\n946:      *\n947:      * @param metadataSnapshot  The current cluster metadata\n948:      * @param nodes             The list of node to drain\n949:      * @param maxSize           The maximum number of bytes to drain\n950:      * @param now               The current unix time in milliseconds\n951:      * @return A list of {@link ProducerBatch} for each node specified with total size less than the\n952:      * requested maxSize.\n953:      */\n954:     public Map<Integer, List<ProducerBatch>> drain(MetadataSnapshot metadataSnapshot, Set<Node> nodes, int maxSize, long now) {\n955:         if (nodes.isEmpty())\n956:             return Collections.emptyMap();\n957: \n958:         Map<Integer, List<ProducerBatch>> batches = new HashMap<>();\n959:         for (Node node : nodes) {\n960:             List<ProducerBatch> ready = drainBatchesForOneNode(metadataSnapshot, node, maxSize, now);\n961:             batches.put(node.id(), ready);\n962:         }\n963:         return batches;\n964:     }\n965: \n966:     public void updateNodeLatencyStats(Integer nodeId, long nowMs, boolean canDrain) {\n967:         // Don't bother with updating stats if the feature is turned off.\n968:         if (partitionAvailabilityTimeoutMs <= 0)\n969:             return;\n970: \n971:         // When the sender gets a node (returned by the ready() function) that has data to send\n972:         // but the node is not ready (and so we cannot drain the data), we only update the\n973:         // ready time, then the difference would reflect for how long a node wasn't ready\n974:         // to send the data. until the send is complete\n1067:      */\n1068:     public void awaitFlushCompletion() throws InterruptedException {\n1069:         try {\n1070:             // Obtain a copy of all of the incomplete ProduceRequestResult(s) at the time of the flush.\n1071:             // We must be careful not to hold a reference to the ProduceBatch(s) so that garbage\n1072:             // collection can occur on the contents.\n1073:             // The sender will remove ProducerBatch(s) from the original incomplete collection.\n1074:             //\n1075:             // We use awaitAllDependents() here instead of await() to ensure that if any batch\n1076:             // was split into multiple batches, we wait for all the split batches to complete.\n1077:             // This is required to guarantee that all records sent before flush()\n1078:             // must be fully complete, including records in split batches.\n1079:             for (ProduceRequestResult result : this.incomplete.requestResults())\n1080:                 result.awaitAllDependents();\n1081:         } finally {\n1082:             this.flushesInProgress.decrementAndGet();\n1083:         }\n1084:     }\n1085: \n1086:     /**\n1087:      * Check whether there are any pending batches (whether sent or unsent).\n1088:      */\n1089:     public boolean hasIncomplete() {\n1090:         return !this.incomplete.isEmpty();\n1091:     }\n1092: \n1093:     /**\n1094:      * This function is only called when sender is closed forcefully. It will fail all the\n1095:      * incomplete batches and return.\n1096:      */\n1097:     public void abortIncompleteBatches() {\n1098:         // We need to keep aborting the incomplete batch until no thread is trying to append to\n1099:         // 1. Avoid losing batches.\n1100:         // 2. Free up memory in case appending threads are blocked on buffer full.\n1101:         // This is a tight loop but should be able to get through very quickly.\n1102:         do {\n1103:             abortBatches();\n1104:         } while (appendsInProgress());\n1105:         // After this point, no thread will append any messages because they will see the close\n1106:         // flag set. java.util.concurrent.TimeUnit;\\n97: import java.util.concurrent.atomic.AtomicReference;\\n98: \\n99: \\n100: /**\\n101:  * A Kafka client that publishes records to the Kafka cluster.\\n102:  * <P>\\n103:  * The producer is <i>thread safe</i> and sharing a single producer instance across threads will generally be faster than\\n104:  * having multiple instances.\\n105:  * <p>\\n106:  * Here is a simple example of using the producer to send records with strings containing sequential numbers as the key/value\\n107:  * pairs.\\n108:  * <pre>\\n109:  * {@code\\n110:  * Properties props = new Properties();\\n111:  * props.put(\\\"bootstrap.servers\\\", \\\"localhost:9092\\\");\\n112:  * props.put(\\\"linger.ms\\\", 1);\\n113:  * props.put(\\\"key.serializer\\\", \\\"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringSerializer\\\");\\n114:  * props.put(\\\"value.serializer\\\", \\\"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringSerializer\\\");\\n115:  *\\n116:  * Producer<String, String> producer = new KafkaProducer<>(props);\\n117:  * for (int i = 0; i < 100; i++)\\n118:  *     producer.send(new ProducerRecord<String, String>(\\\"my-topic\\\", Integer.toString(i), Integer.toString(i)));\\n119:  *\\n120:  * producer.close();\\n121:  * }</pre>\\n122:  * <p>\\n123:  * The producer consists of a pool of buffer space that holds records that haven't yet been transmitted to the server\\n124:  * as well as a background I/O thread that is responsible for turning these records into requests and transmitting them\\n125:  * to the cluster. Failure to close the producer after use will leak these resources.\\n126:  * <p>\\n127:  * The {@link #send(ProducerRecord) send()} method is asynchronous. When called, it adds the record to a buffer of pending record sends\\n128:  * and immediately returns. This allows the producer to batch together individual records for efficiency.\\n129:  * <p>\\n130:  * The <code>acks</code> config controls the criteria under which requests are considered complete. The default setting \\\"all\\\"\\n131:  * will result in blocking on the full commit of the record, the slowest but most durable setting.\\n132:  * <p>\\n133:  * If the request fails, the producer can automatically retry. The <code>retries</code> setting defaults to <code>Integer.MAX_VALUE</code>, and\\n134:  * it's recommended to use <code>delivery.timeout.ms</code> to control retry behavior, instead of <code>retries</code>.\\n135:  * <p>\\n136:  * The producer maintains buffers of unsent records for each partition. These buffers are of a size specified by\\n137:  * the <code>batch.size</code> config. Making this larger can result in more batching, but requires more memory (since we will\\n138:  * generally have one of these buffers for each active partition).\\n139:  * <p>\\n140:  * By default a buffer is available to send immediately even if there is additional unused space in the buffer. However if you\\n141:  * want to reduce the number of requests you can set <code>linger.ms</code> to something greater than 0. This will\\n142:  * instruct the producer to wait up to that number of milliseconds before sending a request in hope that more records will\\n143:  * arrive to fill up the same batch. This is analogous to Nagle's algorithm in TCP. For example, in the code snippet above,\\n144:  * likely all 100 records would be sent in a single request since we set our linger time to 1 millisecond. However this setting\\n145:  * would add 1 millisecond of latency to our request waiting for more records to arrive if we didn't fill up the buffer. Note that\\n146:  * records that arrive close together in time will generally batch together even with <code>linger.ms=0</code>. So, under heavy load,\\n147:  * batching will occur regardless of the linger configuration; however setting this to something larger than 0 can lead to fewer, more\\n148:  * efficient requests when not under maximal load at the cost of a small amount of latency.\\n149:  * <p>\\n150:  * The <code>buffer.memory</code> controls the total amount of memory available to the producer for buffering. If records\\n151:  * are sent faster than they can be transmitted to the server then this buffer space will be exhausted. When the buffer space is\\n152:  * exhausted additional send calls will block. The threshold for time to block is determined by <code>max.block.ms</code> after which it returns\\n153:  * a failed future with BufferExhaustedException.\\n154:  * <p>\\n155:  * The <code>key.serializer</code> and <code>value.serializer</code> instruct how to turn the key and value objects the user provides with\\n156:  * their <code>ProducerRecord</code> into bytes. You can use the included {@link org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.ByteArraySerializer} or\\n157:  * {@link org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringSerializer} for simple byte or string types.\\n158:  * <p>\\n159:  * From Kafka 0.11, the KafkaProducer supports two additional modes: the idempotent producer and the transactional producer.\\n160:  * The idempotent producer strengthens Kafka's delivery semantics from at least once to exactly once delivery. In particular\\n161:  * producer retries will no longer introduce duplicates. The transactional producer allows an application to send messages\\n162:  * to multiple partitions (and topics!) atomically.\\n163:  * </p>\\n164:  * <p>\\n165:  * From Kafka 3.0, the <code>enable.idempotence</code> configuration defaults to true. When enabling idempotence,\\n166:  * <code>retries</code> config will default to <code>Integer.MAX_VALUE</code> and the <code>acks</code> config will\\n167:  * default to <code>all</code>. There are no API changes for the idempotent producer, so existing applications will\\n168:  * not need to be modified to take advantage of this feature.\\n169:  * </p>\\n170:  * <p>\\n171:  * To take advantage of the idempotent producer, it is imperative to avoid application level re-sends since these cannot\\n172:  * be de-duplicated. As such, if an application enables idempotence, it is recommended to leave the <code>retries</code>\\n173:  * config unset, as it will be defaulted to <code>Integer.MAX_VALUE</code>. Additionally, if a {@link #send(ProducerRecord)}\\n174:  * returns an error even with infinite retries (for instance if the message expires in the buffer before being sent),\\n175:  * then it is recommended to shut down the producer and check the contents of the last produced message to ensure that\\n176:  * it is not duplicated. Finally, the producer can only guarantee idempotence for messages sent within a single session.\\n177:  * </p>\\n178:  * <p>To use the transactional producer and the attendant APIs, you must set the <code>transactional.id</code>\\n179:  * configuration property. If the <code>transactional.id</code> is set, idempotence is automatically enabled along with\\n180:  * the producer configs which idempotence depends on. Further, topics which are included in transactions should be configured\\n181:  * for durability. In particular, the <code>replication.factor</code> should be at least <code>3</code>, and the\\n182:  * <code>min.insync.replicas</code> for these topics should be set to 2. Finally, in order for transactional guarantees\\n183:  * to be realized from end-to-end, the consumers must be configured to read only committed messages as well.\\n184:  * </p>\\n185:  * <p>\\n186:  * The purpose of the <code>transactional.id</code> is to enable transaction recovery across multiple sessions of a\\n187:  * single producer instance. It would typically be derived from the shard identifier in a partitioned, stateful, application.\\n188:  * As such, it should be unique to each producer instance running within a partitioned application.\\n189:  * </p>\\n190:  * <p>All the new transactional APIs are blocking and will throw exceptions on failure. The example\\n191:  * below illustrates how the new APIs are meant to be used. It is similar to the example above, except that all\\n192:  * 100 messages are part of a single transaction.\\n193:  * </p>\\n194:  * <p>\\n195:  * <pre>\\n196:  * {@code\\n197:  * Properties props = new Properties();\\n198:  * props.put(\\\"bootstrap.servers\\\", \\\"localhost:9092\\\");\\n199:  * props.put(\\\"transactional.id\\\", \\\"my-transactional-id\\\");\\n200:  * Producer<String, String> producer = new KafkaProducer<>(props, new StringSerializer(), new StringSerializer());\\n201:  *\\n202:  * producer.initTransactions();\\n203:  *\\n204:  * try {\\n205:  *     producer.beginTransaction();\\n206:  *     for (int i = 0; i < 100; i++)\\n207:  *         producer.send(new ProducerRecord<>(\\\"my-topic\\\", Integer.toString(i), Integer.toString(i)));\\n208:  *     producer.commitTransaction();\\n209:  * } catch (ProducerFencedException | OutOfOrderSequenceException | AuthorizationException e) {\\n210:  *     // We can't recover from these exceptions, so our only option is to close the producer and exit.\\n211:  *     producer.close();\\n212:  * } catch (KafkaException e) {\\n213:  *     // For all other exceptions, just abort the transaction and try again.\\n214:  *     producer.abortTransaction();\\n215:  * }\\n216:  * producer.close();\\n217:  * } </pre>\\n218:  * </p>\\n219:  * <p>\\n220:  * As is hinted at in the example, there can be only one open transaction per producer. All messages sent between the\\n221:  * {@link #beginTransaction()} and {@link #commitTransaction()} calls will be part of a single transaction. When the\\n222:  * <code>transactional.id</code> is specified, all messages sent by the producer must be part of a transaction.\\n223:  * </p>\\n224:  * <p>\\n225:  * The transactional producer uses exceptions to communicate error states. In particular, it is not required\\n226:  * to specify callbacks for <code>producer.send()</code> or to call <code>.get()</code> on the returned Future: a\\n227:  * <code>KafkaException</code> would be thrown if any of the\\n228:  * <code>producer.send()</code> or transactional calls hit an irrecoverable error during a transaction. See the {@link #send(ProducerRecord)}\\n229:  * documentation for more details about detecting errors from a transactional send.\\n230:  * </p>\\n231:  * </p>By calling\\n232:  * <code>producer.abortTransaction()</code> upon receiving a <code>KafkaException</code> we can ensure that any\\n233:  * successful writes are marked as aborted, hence keeping the transactional guarantees.\\n234:  * </p>\\n235:  * <p>\\n236:  * This client can communicate with brokers that are version 0.10.0 or newer. Older or newer brokers may not support\\n237:  * certain client features.  For instance, the transactional APIs need broker versions 0.11.0 or later. You will receive an\\n238:  * <code>UnsupportedVersionException</code> when invoking an API that is not available in the running broker version.\\n239:  * </p>\\n240:  */\\n241: public class org.apache.kafka.common.utils.Time;\\n80: import org.apache.kafka.common.utils.Timer;\\n81: import org.apache.kafka.common.utils.Utils;\\n82: \\n83: import org.slf4j.Logger;\\n84: \\n85: import java.net.InetSocketAddress;\\n86: import java.time.Duration;\\n87: import java.util.Arrays;\\n88: import java.util.Collections;\\n89: import java.util.List;\\n90: import java.util.Map;\\n91: import java.util.Objects;\\n92: import java.util.Optional;\\n93: import java.util.Properties;\\n94: import java.util.concurrent.ExecutionException;\\n95: import java.util.concurrent.Future;\\n96: import java.util.concurrent.TimeUnit;\\n97: import java.util.concurrent.atomic.AtomicReference;\\n98: \\n99: \\n100: /**\\n101:  * A Kafka client that publishes records to the Kafka cluster.\\n102:  * <P>\\n103:  * The producer is <i>thread safe</i> and sharing a single producer instance across threads will generally be faster than\\n104:  * having multiple instances.\\n105:  * <p>\\n106:  * Here is a simple example of using the producer to send records with strings containing sequential numbers as the key/value\\n107:  * pairs.\\n108:  * <pre>\\n109:  * {@code\\n110:  * Properties props = new Properties();\\n111:  * props.put(\\\"bootstrap.servers\\\", \\\"localhost:9092\\\");\\n112:  * props.put(\\\"linger.ms\\\", 1);\\n113:  * props.put(\\\"key.serializer\\\", \\\"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringSerializer\\\");\\n114:  * props.put(\\\"value.serializer\\\", \\\"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringSerializer\\\");\\n115:  *\\n116:  * Producer<String, String> producer = new KafkaProducer<>(props);\\n117:  * for (int i = 0; i < 100; i++)\\n118:  *     producer.send(new ProducerRecord<String, String>(\\\"my-topic\\\", Integer.toString(i), Integer.toString(i)));\\n119:  *\\n120:  * producer.close();\\n121:  * }</pre>\\n122:  * <p>\\n123:  * The producer consists of a pool of buffer space that holds records that haven't yet been transmitted to the server\\n124:  * as well as a background I/O thread that is responsible for turning these records into requests and transmitting them\\n125:  * to the cluster. Failure to close the producer after use will leak these resources.\\n126:  * <p>\\n127:  * The {@link #send(ProducerRecord) send()} method is asynchronous. When called, it adds the record to a buffer of pending record sends\\n128:  * and immediately returns. This allows the producer to batch together individual records for efficiency.\\n129:  * <p>\\n130:  * The <code>acks</code> config controls the criteria under which requests are considered complete. The default setting \\\"all\\\"\\n131:  * will result in blocking on the full commit of the record, the slowest but most durable setting.\\n132:  * <p>\\n133:  * If the request fails, the producer can automatically retry. The <code>retries</code> setting defaults to <code>Integer.MAX_VALUE</code>, and\\n134:  * it's recommended to use <code>delivery.timeout.ms</code> to control retry behavior, instead of <code>retries</code>.\\n135:  * <p>\\n136:  * The producer maintains buffers of unsent records for each partition. These buffers are of a size specified by\\n137:  * the <code>batch.size</code> config. Making this larger can result in more batching, but requires more memory (since we will\\n138:  * generally have one of these buffers for each active partition).\\n139:  * <p>\\n140:  * By default a buffer is available to send immediately even if there is additional unused space in the buffer. However if you\\n141:  * want to reduce the number of requests you can set <code>linger.ms</code> to something greater than 0. This will\\n142:  * instruct the producer to wait up to that number of milliseconds before sending a request in hope that more records will\\n143:  * arrive to fill up the same batch. This is analogous to Nagle's algorithm in TCP. For example, in the code snippet above,\\n144:  * likely all 100 records would be sent in a single request since we set our linger time to 1 millisecond. However this setting\\n145:  * would add 1 millisecond of latency to our request waiting for more records to arrive if we didn't fill up the buffer. Note that\\n146:  * records that arrive close together in time will generally batch together even with <code>linger.ms=0</code>. So, under heavy load,\\n147:  * batching will occur regardless of the linger configuration; however setting this to something larger than 0 can lead to fewer, more\\n148:  * efficient requests when not under maximal load at the cost of a small amount of latency.\\n149:  * <p>\\n150:  * The <code>buffer.memory</code> controls the total amount of memory available to the producer for buffering. If records\\n151:  * are sent faster than they can be transmitted to the server then this buffer space will be exhausted. When the buffer space is\\n152:  * exhausted additional send calls will block. The threshold for time to block is determined by <code>max.block.ms</code> after which it returns\\n153:  * a failed future with BufferExhaustedException.\\n154:  * <p>\\n155:  * The <code>key.serializer</code> and <code>value.serializer</code> instruct how to turn the key and value objects the user provides with\\n156:  * their <code>ProducerRecord</code> into bytes. You can use the included {@link org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.ByteArraySerializer} or\\n157:  * {@link org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringSerializer} for simple byte or string types.\\n158:  * <p>\\n159:  * From Kafka 0.11, the KafkaProducer supports two additional modes: the idempotent producer and the transactional producer.\\n160:  * The idempotent producer strengthens Kafka's delivery semantics from at least once to exactly once delivery. In particular\\n161:  * producer retries will no longer introduce duplicates. The transactional producer allows an application to send messages\\n162:  * to multiple partitions (and topics!) atomically.\\n163:  * </p>\\n164:  * <p>\\n165:  * From Kafka 3.0, the <code>enable.idempotence</code> configuration defaults to true. When enabling idempotence,\\n166:  * <code>retries</code> config will default to <code>Integer.MAX_VALUE</code> and the <code>acks</code> config will\\n167:  * default to <code>all</code>. There are no API changes for the idempotent producer, so existing applications will\\n168:  * not need to be modified to take advantage of this feature.\\n169:  * </p>\\n170:  * <p>\\n171:  * To take advantage of the idempotent producer, it is imperative to avoid application level re-sends since these cannot\\n172:  * be de-duplicated. As such, if an application enables idempotence, it is recommended to leave the <code>retries</code>\\n173:  * config unset, as it will be defaulted to <code>Integer.MAX_VALUE</code>. Additionally, if a {@link #send(ProducerRecord)}\\n174:  * returns an error even with infinite retries (for instance if the message expires in the buffer before being sent),\\n175:  * then it is recommended to shut down the producer and check the contents of the last produced message to ensure that\\n176:  * it is not duplicated. Finally, the producer can only guarantee idempotence for messages sent within a single session.\\n177:  * </p>\\n178:  * <p>To use the transactional producer and the attendant APIs, you must set the <code>transactional.id</code>\\n179:  * configuration property. If the <code>transactional.id</code> is set, idempotence is automatically enabled along with\\n180:  * the producer configs which idempotence depends on. Further, topics which are included in transactions should be configured\\n181:  * for durability. In particular, the <code>replication.factor</code> should be at least <code>3</code>, and the\\n182:  * <code>min.insync.replicas</code> for these topics should be set to 2. Finally, in order for transactional guarantees\\n183:  * to be realized from end-to-end, the consumers must be configured to read only committed messages as well.\\n184:  * </p>\\n185:  * <p>\\n186:  * The purpose of the <code>transactional.id</code> is to enable transaction recovery across multiple sessions of a\\n187:  * single producer instance. It would typically be derived from the shard identifier in a partitioned, stateful, application.\\n188:  * As such, it should be unique to each producer instance running within a partitioned application.\\n189:  * </p>\\n190:  * <p>All the new transactional APIs are blocking and will throw exceptions on failure. The example\\n191:  * below illustrates how the new APIs are meant to be used. It is similar to the example above, except that all\\n192:  * 100 messages are part of a single transaction.\\n193:  * </p>\\n194:  * <p>\\n195:  * <pre>\\n196:  * {@code\\n197:  * Properties props = new Properties();\\n198:  * props.put(\\\"bootstrap.servers\\\", \\\"localhost:9092\\\");\\n199:  * props.put(\\\"transactional.id\\\", \\\"my-transactional-id\\\");\\n200:  * Producer<String, String> producer = new KafkaProducer<>(props, new StringSerializer(), new StringSerializer());\\n201:  *\\n202:  * producer.initTransactions();\\n203:  *\\n204:  * try {\\n205:  *     producer.beginTransaction();\\n206:  *     for (int i = 0; i < 100; i++)\\n207:  *         producer.send(new ProducerRecord<>(\\\"my-topic\\\", Integer.toString(i), Integer.toString(i)));\\n208:  *     producer.commitTransaction();\\n209:  * } catch (ProducerFencedException | OutOfOrderSequenceException | AuthorizationException e) {\\n210:  *     // We can't recover from these exceptions, so our only option is to close the producer and exit.\\n211:  *     producer.close();\\n212:  * } catch (KafkaException e) {\\n213:  *     // For all other exceptions, just abort the transaction and try again.\\n214:  *     producer.abortTransaction();\\n215:  * }\\n216:  * producer.close();\\n217:  * } </pre>\\n218:  * </p>\\n219:  * <p>\\n220:  * As is hinted at in the example, there can be only one open transaction per producer. All messages sent between the\\n221:  * {@link #beginTransaction()} and {@link #commitTransaction()} calls will be part of a single transaction. When the\\n222:  * <code>transactional.id</code> is specified, all messages sent by the producer must be part of a transaction.\\n223:  * </p>\\n224:  * <p>\\n225:  * The transactional producer uses exceptions to communicate error states. In particular, it is not required\\n226:  * to specify callbacks for <code>producer.send()</code> or to call <code>.get()</code> on the returned Future: a\\n227:  * <code>KafkaException</code> would be thrown if any of the\\n228:  * <code>producer.send()</code> or transactional calls hit an irrecoverable error during a transaction. See the {@link #send(ProducerRecord)}\\n229:  * documentation for more details about detecting errors from a transactional send.\\n230:  * </p>\\n231:  * </p>By calling\\n232:  * <code>producer.abortTransaction()</code> upon receiving a <code>KafkaException</code> we can ensure that any\\n233:  * successful writes are marked as aborted, hence keeping the transactional guarantees.\\n234:  * </p>\\n235:  * <p>\\n236:  * This client can communicate with brokers that are version 0.10.0 or newer. Older or newer brokers may not support\\n237:  * certain client features.  For instance, the transactional APIs need broker versions 0.11.0 or later. You will receive an\\n238:  * <code>UnsupportedVersionException</code> when invoking an API that is not available in the running broker version.\\n239:  * </p>\\n240:  */\\n241: public class org.apache.kafka.common.utils.Time;\n80: import org.apache.kafka.common.utils.Timer;\n81: import org.apache.kafka.common.utils.Utils;\n82: \n83: import org.slf4j.Logger;\n84: \n85: import java.net.InetSocketAddress;\n86: import java.time.Duration;\n87: import java.util.Arrays;\n88: import java.util.Collections;\n89: import java.util.List;\n90: import java.util.Map;\n91: import java.util.Objects;\n92: import java.util.Optional;\n93: import java.util.Properties;\n94: import java.util.concurrent.ExecutionException;\n95: import java.util.concurrent.Future;\n96: import java.util.concurrent.TimeUnit;\n97: import java.util.concurrent.atomic.AtomicReference;\n98: \n99: \n100: /**\n101:  * A Kafka client that publishes records to the Kafka cluster.\n102:  * <P>\n103:  * The producer is <i>thread safe</i> and sharing a single producer instance across threads will generally be faster than\n104:  * having multiple instances.\n105:  * <p>\n106:  * Here is a simple example of using the producer to send records with strings containing sequential numbers as the key/value\n107:  * pairs.\n108:  * <pre>\n109:  * {@code\n110:  * Properties props = new Properties();\n111:  * props.put(\"bootstrap.servers\", \"localhost:9092\");\n112:  * props.put(\"linger.ms\", 1);\n113:  * props.put(\"key.serializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringSerializer\");\n114:  * props.put(\"value.serializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringSerializer\");\n115:  *\n116:  * Producer<String, String> producer = new KafkaProducer<>(props);\n117:  * for (int i = 0; i < 100; i++)\n118:  *     producer.send(new ProducerRecord<String, String>(\"my-topic\", Integer.toString(i), Integer.toString(i)));\n119:  *\n120:  * producer.close();\n121:  * }</pre>\n122:  * <p>\n123:  * The producer consists of a pool of buffer space that holds records that haven't yet been transmitted to the server\n124:  * as well as a background I/O thread that is responsible for turning these records into requests and transmitting them\n125:  * to the cluster. Failure to close the producer after use will leak these resources.\n126:  * <p>\n127:  * The {@link #send(ProducerRecord) send()} method is asynchronous. When called, it adds the record to a buffer of pending record sends\n128:  * and immediately returns. This allows the producer to batch together individual records for efficiency.\n129:  * <p>\n130:  * The <code>acks</code> config controls the criteria under which requests are considered complete. The default setting \"all\"\n131:  * will result in blocking on the full commit of the record, the slowest but most durable setting.\n132:  * <p>\n133:  * If the request fails, the producer can automatically retry. The <code>retries</code> setting defaults to <code>Integer.MAX_VALUE</code>, and\n134:  * it's recommended to use <code>delivery.timeout.ms</code> to control retry behavior, instead of <code>retries</code>.\n135:  * <p>\n136:  * The producer maintains buffers of unsent records for each partition. These buffers are of a size specified by\n137:  * the <code>batch.size</code> config. Making this larger can result in more batching, but requires more memory (since we will\n138:  * generally have one of these buffers for each active partition).\n139:  * <p>\n140:  * By default a buffer is available to send immediately even if there is additional unused space in the buffer. However if you\n141:  * want to reduce the number of requests you can set <code>linger.ms</code> to something greater than 0. This will\n142:  * instruct the producer to wait up to that number of milliseconds before sending a request in hope that more records will\n143:  * arrive to fill up the same batch. This is analogous to Nagle's algorithm in TCP. For example, in the code snippet above,\n144:  * likely all 100 records would be sent in a single request since we set our linger time to 1 millisecond. However this setting\n145:  * would add 1 millisecond of latency to our request waiting for more records to arrive if we didn't fill up the buffer. Note that\n146:  * records that arrive close together in time will generally batch together even with <code>linger.ms=0</code>. So, under heavy load,\n147:  * batching will occur regardless of the linger configuration; however setting this to something larger than 0 can lead to fewer, more\n148:  * efficient requests when not under maximal load at the cost of a small amount of latency.\n149:  * <p>\n150:  * The <code>buffer.memory</code> controls the total amount of memory available to the producer for buffering. If records\n151:  * are sent faster than they can be transmitted to the server then this buffer space will be exhausted. When the buffer space is\n152:  * exhausted additional send calls will block. The threshold for time to block is determined by <code>max.block.ms</code> after which it returns\n153:  * a failed future with BufferExhaustedException.\n154:  * <p>\n155:  * The <code>key.serializer</code> and <code>value.serializer</code> instruct how to turn the key and value objects the user provides with\n156:  * their <code>ProducerRecord</code> into bytes. You can use the included {@link org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.ByteArraySerializer} or\n157:  * {@link org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringSerializer} for simple byte or string types.\n158:  * <p>\n159:  * From Kafka 0.11, the KafkaProducer supports two additional modes: the idempotent producer and the transactional producer.\n160:  * The idempotent producer strengthens Kafka's delivery semantics from at least once to exactly once delivery. In particular\n161:  * producer retries will no longer introduce duplicates. The transactional producer allows an application to send messages\n162:  * to multiple partitions (and topics!) atomically.\n163:  * </p>\n164:  * <p>\n165:  * From Kafka 3.0, the <code>enable.idempotence</code> configuration defaults to true. When enabling idempotence,\n166:  * <code>retries</code> config will default to <code>Integer.MAX_VALUE</code> and the <code>acks</code> config will\n167:  * default to <code>all</code>. There are no API changes for the idempotent producer, so existing applications will\n168:  * not need to be modified to take advantage of this feature.\n169:  * </p>\n170:  * <p>\n171:  * To take advantage of the idempotent producer, it is imperative to avoid application level re-sends since these cannot\n172:  * be de-duplicated. As such, if an application enables idempotence, it is recommended to leave the <code>retries</code>\n173:  * config unset, as it will be defaulted to <code>Integer.MAX_VALUE</code>. Additionally, if a {@link #send(ProducerRecord)}\n174:  * returns an error even with infinite retries (for instance if the message expires in the buffer before being sent),\n175:  * then it is recommended to shut down the producer and check the contents of the last produced message to ensure that\n176:  * it is not duplicated. Finally, the producer can only guarantee idempotence for messages sent within a single session.\n177:  * </p>\n178:  * <p>To use the transactional producer and the attendant APIs, you must set the <code>transactional.id</code>\n179:  * configuration property. If the <code>transactional.id</code> is set, idempotence is automatically enabled along with\n180:  * the producer configs which idempotence depends on. Further, topics which are included in transactions should be configured\n181:  * for durability. In particular, the <code>replication.factor</code> should be at least <code>3</code>, and the\n182:  * <code>min.insync.replicas</code> for these topics should be set to 2. Finally, in order for transactional guarantees\n183:  * to be realized from end-to-end, the consumers must be configured to read only committed messages as well.\n184:  * </p>\n185:  * <p>\n186:  * The purpose of the <code>transactional.id</code> is to enable transaction recovery across multiple sessions of a\n187:  * single producer instance. It would typically be derived from the shard identifier in a partitioned, stateful, application.\n188:  * As such, it should be unique to each producer instance running within a partitioned application.\n189:  * </p>\n190:  * <p>All the new transactional APIs are blocking and will throw exceptions on failure. The example\n191:  * below illustrates how the new APIs are meant to be used. It is similar to the example above, except that all\n192:  * 100 messages are part of a single transaction.\n193:  * </p>\n194:  * <p>\n195:  * <pre>\n196:  * {@code\n197:  * Properties props = new Properties();\n198:  * props.put(\"bootstrap.servers\", \"localhost:9092\");\n199:  * props.put(\"transactional.id\", \"my-transactional-id\");\n200:  * Producer<String, String> producer = new KafkaProducer<>(props, new StringSerializer(), new StringSerializer());\n201:  *\n202:  * producer.initTransactions();\n203:  *\n204:  * try {\n205:  *     producer.beginTransaction();\n206:  *     for (int i = 0; i < 100; i++)\n207:  *         producer.send(new ProducerRecord<>(\"my-topic\", Integer.toString(i), Integer.toString(i)));\n208:  *     producer.commitTransaction();\n209:  * } catch (ProducerFencedException | OutOfOrderSequenceException | AuthorizationException e) {\n210:  *     // We can't recover from these exceptions, so our only option is to close the producer and exit.\n211:  *     producer.close();\n212:  * } catch (KafkaException e) {\n213:  *     // For all other exceptions, just abort the transaction and try again.\n214:  *     producer.abortTransaction();\n215:  * }\n216:  * producer.close();\n217:  * } </pre>\n218:  * </p>\n219:  * <p>\n220:  * As is hinted at in the example, there can be only one open transaction per producer. All messages sent between the\n221:  * {@link #beginTransaction()} and {@link #commitTransaction()} calls will be part of a single transaction. When the\n222:  * <code>transactional.id</code> is specified, all messages sent by the producer must be part of a transaction.\n223:  * </p>\n224:  * <p>\n225:  * The transactional producer uses exceptions to communicate error states. In particular, it is not required\n226:  * to specify callbacks for <code>producer.send()</code> or to call <code>.get()</code> on the returned Future: a\n227:  * <code>KafkaException</code> would be thrown if any of the\n228:  * <code>producer.send()</code> or transactional calls hit an irrecoverable error during a transaction. See the {@link #send(ProducerRecord)}\n229:  * documentation for more details about detecting errors from a transactional send.\n230:  * </p>\n231:  * </p>By calling\n232:  * <code>producer.abortTransaction()</code> upon receiving a <code>KafkaException</code> we can ensure that any\n233:  * successful writes are marked as aborted, hence keeping the transactional guarantees.\n234:  * </p>\n235:  * <p>\n236:  * This client can communicate with brokers that are version 0.10.0 or newer. Older or newer brokers may not support\n237:  * certain client features.  For instance, the transactional APIs need broker versions 0.11.0 or later. You will receive an\n238:  * <code>UnsupportedVersionException</code> when invoking an API that is not available in the running broker version.\n239:  * </p>\n240:  */\n241: public class KafkaProducer<K, V> implements Producer<K, V> {\n242: \n243:     private final Logger log;\n244:     private static final String JMX_PREFIX = \"kafka.producer\";\n245:     public static final String NETWORK_THREAD_PREFIX = \"kafka-producer-network-thread\";\n246:     public static final String PRODUCER_METRIC_GROUP_NAME = \"producer-metrics\";\n247: \n248:     private final String clientId;\n249:     // Visible for testing\n250:     final Metrics metrics;\n251:     private final KafkaProducerMetrics producerMetrics;\n252:     private final Plugin<Partitioner> partitionerPlugin;\n253:     private final int maxRequestSize;\n254:     private final long totalMemorySize;\n255:     private final ProducerMetadata metadata;\n256:     private final RecordAccumulator accumulator;\n257:     private final Sender sender;\n258:     private final Sender.SenderThread ioThread;\n259:     private final Compression compression;\n260:     private final Sensor errors;\n261:     private final Time time;\n262:     private final Plugin<Serializer<K>> keySerializerPlugin;\n263:     private final Plugin<Serializer<V>> valueSerializerPlugin;\n264:     private final ProducerConfig producerConfig;\n265:     private final long maxBlockTimeMs;\n266:     private final boolean partitionerIgnoreKeys;\n267:     private final ProducerInterceptors<K, V> interceptors;\n268:     private final ApiVersions apiVersions;\n269:     private final TransactionManager transactionManager;\n270:     // Init value is needed to avoid NPE in case of exception raised in the constructor\n271:     private Optional<ClientTelemetryReporter> clientTelemetryReporter = Optional.empty();\n272: \n273:     /**\n274:      * A producer is instantiated by providing a set of key-value pairs as configuration. Its core data structure is a `ConcurrentMap<TopicPartition, Deque<ProducerBatch>>`, and its key methods (`ready()`, `drain()`, `append()`) all operate at batch granularity. Renaming to `BatchAccumulator` better describes the class's true responsibility.\n\n## Files Examined\n\n### Primary Definition\n1. **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java**\n   - Main class definition\n   - Contains inner classes: `RecordAppendResult`, `ReadyCheckResult`, `PartitionerConfig`, `AppendCallbacks`, `NodeLatencyStats`, `TopicInfo`\n   - ~1,268 lines\n   - Rename to: `BatchAccumulator.java`\n\n### Direct Usage (Core Producer Classes)\n2. **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/KafkaProducer.java**\n   - Import: `org.apache.kafka.clients.producer.internals.RecordAccumulator`\n   - Field: `private final RecordAccumulator accumulator` (line 256)\n   - Constructor instantiation: `new RecordAccumulator(...)` (line 426)\n   - Inner class reference: `RecordAccumulator.PartitionerConfig` (line 419)\n\n3. **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java**\n   - Field: `private final RecordAccumulator accumulator` (line 87)\n   - Constructor parameter: `RecordAccumulator accumulator` (line 131)\n   - Inner class usage: `RecordAccumulator.ReadyCheckResult` (line 360)\n\n### Comment References (Non-Functional)\n4. **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/Node.java**\n   - Comment: \"Cache hashCode as it is called in performance sensitive parts of the code (e.g. RecordAccumulator.ready)\" (line 35)\n\n5. **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BuiltInPartitioner.java**\n   - Comment: \"Built-in default partitioner.
